Question 1hard

Which of the following statements is INCORRECT regarding the properties of transition elements?

  1. They exhibit variable oxidation states.
  2. They form colored ions.
  3. They are generally good reducing agents.
  4. They have high melting and boiling points.
Show answer

Answer: They are generally good reducing agents.

Transition elements generally exhibit variable oxidation states due to the involvement of both (n-1)d and ns electrons. They form colored ions due to d-d transitions. They have high melting and boiling points due to strong metallic bonding. However, transition elements, especially in higher oxidation states, tend to act as oxidizing agents rather than reducing agents. For example, KMnO4 and K2Cr2O7 are strong oxidizing agents.

Question 2hard

The rate constant of a first-order reaction is 2.303 × 10⁻³ s⁻¹. What will be the time required for the concentration of the reactant to reduce to 1/10th of its initial value?

  1. 100 s
  2. 230.3 s
  3. 1000 s
  4. 2303 s
Show answer

Answer: 1000 s

For a first-order reaction, the integrated rate law is given by: t = (2.303 / k) * log([A]₀ / [A]). Given k = 2.303 × 10⁻³ s⁻¹ and [A] = [A]₀ / 10. So, t = (2.303 / (2.303 × 10⁻³)) * log([A]₀ / ([A]₀ / 10)) t = (1 / 10⁻³) * log(10) t = 1000 * 1 t = 1000 s.

Question 3hard

Which of the following compounds will NOT give a positive iodoform test?

  1. Ethanol
  2. Propan-2-ol
  3. Propanal
  4. Acetophenone
Show answer

Answer: Propanal

The iodoform test is given by compounds containing a CH₃CO- group or a CH₃CH(OH)- group. Ethanol (CH₃CH₂OH) has a CH₃CH(OH)- group (after oxidation to acetaldehyde). Propan-2-ol (CH₃CH(OH)CH₃) has a CH₃CH(OH)- group. Acetophenone (C₆H₅COCH₃) has a CH₃CO- group. Propanal (CH₃CH₂CHO) does not have either of these groups. It has a CH₃CH₂CO- group, which does not react to give iodoform.

Question 4hard

The correct order of increasing acidic strength for the following compounds is:

  1. Phenol < p-Nitrophenol < p-Cresol
  2. p-Cresol < Phenol < p-Nitrophenol
  3. p-Nitrophenol < Phenol < p-Cresol
  4. Phenol < p-Cresol < p-Nitrophenol
Show answer

Answer: p-Cresol < Phenol < p-Nitrophenol

The acidic strength of phenols is influenced by substituents on the benzene ring. Electron-withdrawing groups (like -NO₂) increase acidity by stabilizing the phenoxide ion through resonance and inductive effects. Electron-donating groups (like -CH₃) decrease acidity by destabilizing the phenoxide ion. p-Nitrophenol has an electron-withdrawing -NO₂ group, making it the most acidic. p-Cresol has an electron-donating -CH₃ group, making it the least acidic. Phenol is in between. Therefore, the order of increasing acidic strength is p-Cresol < Phenol < p-Nitrophenol.

Question 5hard

Which of the following is a characteristic property of lyophilic colloids?

  1. They are easily coagulated by adding small amounts of electrolytes.
  2. They are irreversible in nature.
  3. They are generally less stable than lyophobic colloids.
  4. They are self-stabilizing and do not require stabilizing agents.
Show answer

Answer: They are self-stabilizing and do not require stabilizing agents.

Lyophilic colloids are 'solvent-loving' and are stable due to strong attractive forces between the dispersed phase and the dispersion medium. This strong interaction makes them self-stabilizing and reversible (if the dispersion medium is removed, the dispersed phase can be redispersed). They are not easily coagulated by electrolytes and are generally more stable than lyophobic colloids.

Question 6hard

An organic compound 'A' (C₃H₆O) gives a positive Tollen's test and on oxidation with K₂Cr₂O₇/H⁺ gives 'B' (C₃H₆O₂). Compound 'A' is:

  1. Propanone
  2. Propanal
  3. Propan-1-ol
  4. Propanoic acid
Show answer

Answer: Propanal

The molecular formula C₃H₆O suggests an aldehyde or a ketone. A positive Tollen's test indicates the presence of an aldehyde group (-CHO). Ketones do not give a positive Tollen's test. So, 'A' is an aldehyde. Among the options, Propanal (CH₃CH₂CHO) is an aldehyde with the formula C₃H₆O. On oxidation, aldehydes are converted to carboxylic acids. Propanal on oxidation with K₂Cr₂O₇/H⁺ will give Propanoic acid (CH₃CH₂COOH), which has the formula C₃H₆O₂. Therefore, compound 'A' is Propanal.

Question 7hard

The number of unpaired electrons in the gaseous ion Mn³⁺ (atomic number of Mn = 25) is:

  1. 2
  2. 3
  3. 4
  4. 5
Show answer

Answer: 4

The electronic configuration of Mn (atomic number 25) is [Ar] 3d⁵ 4s². To form Mn³⁺, three electrons are removed. The electrons are first removed from the 4s orbital and then from the 3d orbital. So, Mn³⁺ configuration will be [Ar] 3d⁴. In the 3d⁴ configuration, according to Hund's rule, the four electrons will occupy separate d-orbitals with parallel spins, resulting in 4 unpaired electrons.

Question 8hard

Which of the following is a primary amine?

  1. N,N-Dimethylaniline
  2. Diethylamine
  3. tert-Butylamine
  4. N-Methylaniline
Show answer

Answer: tert-Butylamine

A primary amine (1°) has one alkyl or aryl group attached to the nitrogen atom (-NH₂). N,N-Dimethylaniline is a tertiary amine (C₆H₅N(CH₃)₂). Diethylamine is a secondary amine ((C₂H₅)₂NH). tert-Butylamine ((CH₃)₃C-NH₂) has only one alkyl group (tert-butyl) attached to the nitrogen atom, making it a primary amine. N-Methylaniline is a secondary amine (C₆H₅NHCH₃).

Question 9hard

The osmotic pressure of a solution can be increased by:

  1. Decreasing the temperature.
  2. Increasing the volume of the solution.
  3. Increasing the concentration of the solute.
  4. Adding a non-volatile solvent.
Show answer

Answer: Increasing the concentration of the solute.

The osmotic pressure (π) is given by the formula π = iCRT, where i is the van't Hoff factor, C is the molar concentration of the solute, R is the gas constant, and T is the absolute temperature. From the formula, osmotic pressure is directly proportional to the concentration of the solute (C) and the absolute temperature (T). Therefore, increasing the concentration of the solute will increase the osmotic pressure. Decreasing temperature will decrease it. Increasing the volume of the solution (for a fixed amount of solute) will decrease the concentration and thus decrease osmotic pressure. Adding a non-volatile solvent will decrease the concentration of the solute, thereby decreasing osmotic pressure.

Question 10hard

Which of the following reagents can be used to distinguish between phenol and benzoic acid?

  1. Neutral FeCl₃ solution
  2. Tollen's reagent
  3. Sodium bicarbonate solution
  4. Bromine water
Show answer

Answer: Sodium bicarbonate solution

Phenol is a weak acid, while benzoic acid is a stronger acid. Sodium bicarbonate (NaHCO₃) is a weak base. Benzoic acid, being a stronger acid than carbonic acid, reacts with sodium bicarbonate to produce CO₂ gas with effervescence. Phenol, being a weaker acid than carbonic acid, does not react with sodium bicarbonate. Neutral FeCl₃ solution gives a characteristic violet coloration with phenol, but not with benzoic acid. However, this is a test for phenols, not a general distinction based on acidity. Tollen's reagent is used to detect aldehydes. Neither phenol nor benzoic acid will give a positive Tollen's test. Bromine water reacts with both phenol (decolorizes bromine water and forms a white precipitate of 2,4,6-tribromophenol) and benzoic acid (under specific conditions, but not a clear distinction for acidity). Therefore, sodium bicarbonate solution is the most appropriate reagent to distinguish between phenol and benzoic acid based on their acidic strengths.

Question 11hard

Which of the following is the strongest acid?

  1. CH₃COOH
  2. ClCH₂COOH
  3. Cl₂CHCOOH
  4. Cl₃CCOOH
Show answer

Answer: Cl₃CCOOH

The acidity of carboxylic acids increases with the presence of electron-withdrawing groups (like -Cl) attached to the α-carbon. The more the number of electron-withdrawing groups, the stronger the acid, as they stabilize the carboxylate anion by dispersing the negative charge through inductive effect. Therefore, trichloroacetic acid (Cl₃CCOOH) is the strongest acid among the given options.

Question 12hard

An example of a lyophilic colloid is:

  1. Gold sol
  2. Starch solution
  3. Ferric hydroxide sol
  4. Arsenic sulphide sol
Show answer

Answer: Starch solution

Lyophilic colloids are 'solvent-loving' colloids, meaning they have a strong affinity for the dispersion medium. Starch solution is a classic example of a lyophilic colloid because starch readily dissolves/disperses in water to form a stable colloidal solution. Gold sol, ferric hydroxide sol, and arsenic sulphide sol are examples of lyophobic colloids, which are 'solvent-hating' and require stabilizing agents to prevent coagulation.

Question 13hard

The IUPAC name of the compound [Co(NH₃)₅Cl]Cl₂ is:

  1. Pentamminechlorocobalt(III) chloride
  2. Chloropentamminecobalt(III) chloride
  3. Pentamminechlorocobalt(II) chloride
  4. Chloropentamminecobalt(II) chloride
Show answer

Answer: Pentamminechlorocobalt(III) chloride

In the complex [Co(NH₃)₅Cl]Cl₂, the ligands are five ammonia molecules (ammine) and one chloride ion (chloro). The ligands are named alphabetically, so ammine comes before chloro. The oxidation state of cobalt (Co) needs to be determined. Let the oxidation state of Co be x. NH₃ is neutral (0), Cl inside the coordination sphere is -1, and the two Cl outside are -1 each. So, x + 5(0) + (-1) + 2(-1) = 0, which gives x - 3 = 0, so x = +3. Thus, the IUPAC name is Pentamminechlorocobalt(III) chloride.

Question 14hard

Which of the following reagents will distinguish between propanal and propanone?

  1. Fehling's solution
  2. Grignard reagent
  3. Tollens' reagent
  4. Both A and C
Show answer

Answer: Both A and C

Propanal is an aldehyde, while propanone is a ketone. Aldehydes can be easily oxidized, while ketones are resistant to mild oxidation. Both Fehling's solution and Tollens' reagent are mild oxidizing agents that specifically react with aldehydes to give a positive test (red precipitate for Fehling's, silver mirror for Tollens'). Ketones do not react with these reagents. Therefore, both Fehling's solution and Tollens' reagent can distinguish between propanal and propanone. Grignard reagent reacts with both aldehydes and ketones.

Question 15hard

The molar conductivity of an electrolyte increases with dilution because:

  1. Number of ions per unit volume increases.
  2. Ionic mobility decreases.
  3. Degree of dissociation increases.
  4. Interionic forces of attraction increase.
Show answer

Answer: Degree of dissociation increases.

Molar conductivity (Λm) is defined as the conductivity of a solution containing one mole of electrolyte. For weak electrolytes, with dilution, the degree of dissociation (α) increases, leading to a greater number of ions in the solution. For strong electrolytes, while the number of ions remains constant, the interionic attraction decreases upon dilution, allowing ions to move more freely, thus increasing ionic mobility. However, the most significant factor contributing to the increase in molar conductivity with dilution, especially for weak electrolytes, is the increase in the degree of dissociation. The number of ions per unit volume actually decreases with dilution, and interionic forces decrease, not increase.

Question 16hard

The reaction of an alkyl halide with sodium metal in dry ether is known as:

  1. Wurtz reaction
  2. Fittig reaction
  3. Wurtz-Fittig reaction
  4. Friedel-Crafts reaction
Show answer

Answer: Wurtz reaction

The Wurtz reaction involves the coupling of two alkyl halides (R-X) in the presence of sodium metal and dry ether to form a higher alkane (R-R). The Fittig reaction involves two aryl halides, and the Wurtz-Fittig reaction involves one alkyl halide and one aryl halide. Friedel-Crafts reaction is an electrophilic aromatic substitution reaction.

Question 17hard

Which of the following is a non-reducing sugar?

  1. Glucose
  2. Fructose
  3. Maltose
  4. Sucrose
Show answer

Answer: Sucrose

Reducing sugars are carbohydrates that can act as reducing agents due to the presence of a free aldehyde or ketone group (or hemiacetal/hemiketal group that can open to form an aldehyde/ketone). Glucose, fructose, and maltose all have such groups and are thus reducing sugars. Sucrose, on the other hand, is a disaccharide formed by a glycosidic linkage between the C1 of α-glucose and the C2 of β-fructose. This linkage involves the anomeric carbons of both monosaccharides, meaning neither glucose nor fructose can open up to form a free aldehyde or ketone group. Therefore, sucrose is a non-reducing sugar.

Question 18hard

Which of the following statements is INCORRECT regarding the properties of d-block elements?

  1. They generally form coloured ions.
  2. They exhibit variable oxidation states.
  3. They are good reducing agents.
  4. They form interstitial compounds.
Show answer

Answer: They are good reducing agents.

d-block elements, due to their tendency to lose electrons and form positive ions, are generally good oxidizing agents, not reducing agents. They tend to get oxidized themselves, thereby reducing other species. The other options are characteristic properties of d-block elements.

Question 19hard

An aqueous solution of a substance shows elevation in boiling point. Which of the following statements is true about the solution?

  1. It has a lower vapor pressure than pure solvent.
  2. It has a higher freezing point than pure solvent.
  3. It has a lower osmotic pressure than pure solvent.
  4. It is an ideal solution.
Show answer

Answer: It has a lower vapor pressure than pure solvent.

Elevation in boiling point is a colligative property that occurs when a non-volatile solute is added to a solvent. This addition leads to a decrease in the vapor pressure of the solution compared to the pure solvent. A lower vapor pressure means more energy is required to reach the boiling point, hence elevation in boiling point. The freezing point would be lowered, and osmotic pressure would be higher (for a given concentration) compared to pure solvent. It does not necessarily imply an ideal solution.

Question 20hard

Which of the following reactions is an example of a Sandmeyer reaction?

  1. C₆H₅N₂⁺Cl⁻ + H₂O → C₆H₅OH + N₂ + HCl
  2. C₆H₅N₂⁺Cl⁻ + CuCl/HCl → C₆H₅Cl + N₂
  3. C₆H₅N₂⁺Cl⁻ + KI → C₆H₅I + N₂ + KCl
  4. C₆H₅N₂⁺Cl⁻ + HBF₄ → C₆H₅F + N₂ + BF₃
Show answer

Answer: C₆H₅N₂⁺Cl⁻ + CuCl/HCl → C₆H₅Cl + N₂

The Sandmeyer reaction involves the replacement of the diazonium group (-N₂⁺Cl⁻) by a halogen (Cl, Br) or a cyanide group using copper(I) salts (CuCl/HCl, CuBr/HBr, or CuCN/KCN). Option (B) shows the replacement of the diazonium group by chlorine using CuCl/HCl, which is a classic Sandmeyer reaction. Option (A) is hydrolysis, (C) is a Gattermann reaction variation (without copper powder), and (D) is Balz-Schiemann reaction.

Question 21hard

The primary structure of proteins refers to:

  1. The three-dimensional folding of the polypeptide chain.
  2. The sequence of amino acids in the polypeptide chain.
  3. The arrangement of two or more polypeptide chains.
  4. The formation of α-helix and β-pleated sheet structures.
Show answer

Answer: The sequence of amino acids in the polypeptide chain.

The primary structure of a protein is defined by the specific linear sequence of amino acids linked together by peptide bonds. This sequence is unique to each protein and determines its higher-order structures and biological function. Options (A), (C), and (D) describe tertiary, quaternary, and secondary structures, respectively.

Question 22hard

Which of the following is a diamagnetic complex?

  1. [NiCl₄]²⁻
  2. [Ni(CN)₄]²⁻
  3. [CoF₆]³⁻
  4. [Fe(H₂O)₆]²⁺
Show answer

Answer: [Ni(CN)₄]²⁻

To determine diamagnetism, we need to check for the absence of unpaired electrons. 1. [NiCl₄]²⁻: Ni is in +2 oxidation state (d⁸). Cl⁻ is a weak field ligand. In tetrahedral geometry, it will have 2 unpaired electrons (paramagnetic). 2. [Ni(CN)₄]²⁻: Ni is in +2 oxidation state (d⁸). CN⁻ is a strong field ligand. In square planar geometry, all 8 d-electrons pair up, resulting in 0 unpaired electrons (diamagnetic). 3. [CoF₆]³⁻: Co is in +3 oxidation state (d⁶). F⁻ is a weak field ligand. It will have 4 unpaired electrons (paramagnetic). 4. [Fe(H₂O)₆]²⁺: Fe is in +2 oxidation state (d⁶). H₂O is a weak field ligand. It will have 4 unpaired electrons (paramagnetic).

Question 23hard

What is the product formed when phenol reacts with chloroform in the presence of dilute NaOH, followed by hydrolysis?

  1. Benzaldehyde
  2. Salicylic acid
  3. Salicylaldehyde
  4. Benzoic acid
Show answer

Answer: Salicylaldehyde

This reaction is known as the Reimer-Tiemann reaction. In this reaction, phenol reacts with chloroform (CHCl₃) in the presence of an alkali (NaOH) to introduce an aldehyde group (-CHO) at the ortho position of the phenolic -OH group. The intermediate formed is then hydrolyzed to give salicylaldehyde (o-hydroxybenzaldehyde).

Question 24hard

Which of the following is NOT a characteristic of physisorption?

  1. It is highly specific.
  2. It is reversible.
  3. It involves weak van der Waals forces.
  4. It has a low enthalpy of adsorption.
Show answer

Answer: It is highly specific.

Physisorption (physical adsorption) is non-specific, meaning that a given adsorbent will adsorb almost any gas to some extent. It is reversible, involves weak van der Waals forces, and has a low enthalpy of adsorption (typically 20-40 kJ/mol). Chemisorption, on the other hand, is highly specific.

Question 25hard

The IUPAC name of the compound CH₃-CH(CH₃)-CH₂-CHO is:

  1. 3-Methylbutanal
  2. 2-Methylbutanal
  3. 3-Methylbutyraldehyde
  4. Isovaleraldehyde
Show answer

Answer: 3-Methylbutanal

To name the compound, first identify the longest carbon chain containing the aldehyde group (-CHO). This chain has 4 carbons, making it a 'butanal'. The aldehyde carbon is always numbered as 1. So, the methyl group is at position 3. Therefore, the IUPAC name is 3-Methylbutanal.

Question 26hard

Identify the major product formed when propene reacts with HBr in the presence of a peroxide.

  1. 1-bromopropane
  2. 2-bromopropane
  3. 1,2-dibromopropane
  4. Propane
Show answer

Answer: 1-bromopropane

When propene reacts with HBr in the presence of a peroxide, the reaction follows an anti-Markovnikov's rule mechanism, which is a free radical addition. In this mechanism, the bromine atom adds to the less substituted carbon atom, and the hydrogen atom adds to the more substituted carbon atom, leading to the formation of 1-bromopropane.

Question 27hard

Which of the following is a characteristic feature of an ideal solution?

  1. ΔH_mix > 0
  2. ΔV_mix < 0
  3. Obeys Raoult's Law over the entire range of concentration.
  4. Intermolecular forces between A-B are stronger than A-A and B-B.
Show answer

Answer: Obeys Raoult's Law over the entire range of concentration.

An ideal solution is characterized by obeying Raoult's Law over the entire range of concentration. For an ideal solution, ΔH_mix = 0 and ΔV_mix = 0, meaning there is no heat change or volume change upon mixing. Also, the intermolecular forces between A-B components are similar to those between A-A and B-B components.

Question 28hard

What is the coordination number of the central metal ion in [Co(en)₂Cl₂]Cl?

  1. 2
  2. 4
  3. 6
  4. 8
Show answer

Answer: 6

In the complex [Co(en)₂Cl₂]Cl, 'en' (ethylenediamine) is a bidentate ligand, meaning each 'en' molecule forms two coordinate bonds with the central metal ion. There are two 'en' ligands, so they contribute 2 x 2 = 4 coordinate bonds. The 'Cl' (chloride) ligands are monodentate, and there are two of them, contributing 2 x 1 = 2 coordinate bonds. Therefore, the total coordination number of Co is 4 + 2 = 6.

Question 29hard

Which of the following reagents can be used to distinguish between propanal and propanone?

  1. Tollens' reagent
  2. Fehling's solution
  3. Iodoform test
  4. All of the above
Show answer

Answer: All of the above

Propanal is an aldehyde, and propanone is a ketone. Tollens' reagent and Fehling's solution are used to distinguish aldehydes from ketones, as aldehydes give a positive test (silver mirror/red precipitate) while ketones do not. The iodoform test can also distinguish them because propanone (a methyl ketone) will give a positive iodoform test (yellow precipitate of CHI₃), while propanal will not.

Question 30hard

For a first-order reaction, the time required for 99.9% completion is how many times the half-life of the reaction?

  1. 2
  2. 5
  3. 10
  4. 7
Show answer

Answer: 10

For a first-order reaction, the time for 99.9% completion (t_99.9%) can be calculated using the formula: t = (2.303/k) log(A₀/A). If 99.9% is completed, then A = 0.1% of A₀, so A₀/A = 1000. Thus, t_99.9% = (2.303/k) log(1000) = (2.303/k) * 3. The half-life (t_1/2) for a first-order reaction is (0.693/k). Since 2.303 * 3 ≈ 6.909, and 0.693 * 10 = 6.93, we can approximate t_99.9% ≈ 10 * t_1/2. More precisely, t_99.9% = (3 / 0.301) * t_1/2 ≈ 9.96 * t_1/2, which is approximately 10 times the half-life.

Question 31hard

Which of the following is NOT a characteristic property of colloids?

  1. Tyndall effect
  2. Brownian movement
  3. Homogeneous nature
  4. Electrophoresis
Show answer

Answer: Homogeneous nature

Colloids are heterogeneous mixtures, not homogeneous. They consist of a dispersed phase and a dispersion medium. The other options – Tyndall effect (scattering of light), Brownian movement (random motion of colloidal particles), and electrophoresis (movement of charged colloidal particles under an electric field) – are all characteristic properties of colloids.

Question 32hard

An aqueous solution of a substance gives a white precipitate with AgNO₃ solution. The precipitate is soluble in dilute ammonia solution. The substance could be:

  1. AgCl
  2. AgBr
  3. AgI
  4. Ag₂S
Show answer

Answer: AgCl

This question tests the characteristic reactions of silver halides. Silver chloride (AgCl) forms a white precipitate with AgNO₃ and is soluble in dilute ammonia solution due to the formation of the diamminesilver(I) complex, [Ag(NH₃)₂]⁺. Silver bromide (AgBr) forms a pale yellow precipitate and is sparingly soluble in dilute ammonia. Silver iodide (AgI) forms a yellow precipitate and is insoluble in dilute ammonia. Silver sulfide (Ag₂S) is a black precipitate and is not relevant here.

Question 33hard

Which of the following polymers is a thermoplastic?

  1. Bakelite
  2. Melamine-formaldehyde resin
  3. Polyethylene
  4. Vulcanized rubber
Show answer

Answer: Polyethylene

Thermoplastics are polymers that can be softened on heating and hardened on cooling, and this process can be repeated. They have linear or slightly branched structures. Polyethylene is a thermoplastic. Bakelite and melamine-formaldehyde resin are thermosetting polymers, which undergo irreversible chemical changes on heating and cannot be reshaped. Vulcanized rubber is an elastomer, which has cross-links but is not a thermoplastic.

Question 34hard

The number of atoms per unit cell in a body-centered cubic (BCC) lattice is:

  1. 1
  2. 2
  3. 4
  4. 6
Show answer

Answer: 2

In a body-centered cubic (BCC) lattice, there are 8 atoms at the corners and 1 atom at the body center. Each corner atom contributes 1/8 to the unit cell, so 8 × (1/8) = 1 atom from the corners. The atom at the body center contributes 1 whole atom. Therefore, the total number of atoms per unit cell in a BCC lattice is 1 + 1 = 2.

Question 35hard

Which of the following is an example of a bidentate ligand?

  1. NH₃
  2. Cl⁻
  3. H₂O
  4. Ethylenediamine (en)
Show answer

Answer: Ethylenediamine (en)

A bidentate ligand is a ligand that can form two coordinate bonds with a central metal atom or ion. Ethylenediamine (en), with the formula H₂N-CH₂-CH₂-NH₂, has two nitrogen atoms, each capable of donating a lone pair of electrons to the metal, thus acting as a bidentate ligand. NH₃, Cl⁻, and H₂O are monodentate ligands, meaning they can form only one coordinate bond.

Question 36hard

The IUPAC name of the compound (CH₃)₂CH-CH₂-CHO is:

  1. 2-methylbutanal
  2. 3-methylbutanal
  3. isopentanal
  4. 2,2-dimethylpropanal
Show answer

Answer: 3-methylbutanal

To name the compound (CH₃)₂CH-CH₂-CHO, we first identify the longest carbon chain containing the aldehyde functional group (-CHO). This chain has 4 carbons. The aldehyde carbon is always numbered as 1. So, the chain is -CH₂-CHO. The methyl group is attached to the third carbon from the aldehyde end. Therefore, the IUPAC name is 3-methylbutanal.

Question 37hard

Which of the following compounds will exhibit optical isomerism?

  1. CH3CH2CH2CH3
  2. CH3CH(OH)COOH
  3. CH2=CH-CH2-CH3
  4. CH3-CCl2-CH3
Show answer

Answer: CH3CH(OH)COOH

Optical isomerism (enantiomerism) arises in molecules that are chiral, meaning they are non-superimposable on their mirror images. A common condition for chirality is the presence of a chiral carbon atom, which is a carbon atom bonded to four different groups. In CH3CH(OH)COOH (lactic acid), the central carbon atom is bonded to -CH3, -H, -OH, and -COOH groups, making it a chiral center. The other options lack a chiral carbon atom.

Question 38hard

An aqueous solution of a substance shows elevation in boiling point. Which of the following statements is TRUE about this solution?

  1. Its freezing point will be higher than that of pure solvent.
  2. Its vapor pressure will be higher than that of pure solvent.
  3. It will have a lower osmotic pressure than pure solvent.
  4. Its freezing point will be lower than that of pure solvent.
Show answer

Answer: Its freezing point will be lower than that of pure solvent.

Elevation in boiling point is a colligative property, meaning it depends on the number of solute particles, not their identity. When a non-volatile solute is added to a solvent, it leads to: 1. Elevation in boiling point (boiling point increases). 2. Depression in freezing point (freezing point decreases). 3. Lowering of vapor pressure (vapor pressure decreases). 4. Increase in osmotic pressure. Therefore, if the boiling point is elevated, the freezing point will be lower than that of the pure solvent.

Question 39hard

The correct order of increasing basicity of the following amines in aqueous solution is:

  1. NH3 < CH3NH2 < (CH3)2NH < (CH3)3N
  2. (CH3)3N < NH3 < CH3NH2 < (CH3)2NH
  3. NH3 < (CH3)3N < CH3NH2 < (CH3)2NH
  4. (CH3)3N < CH3NH2 < (CH3)2NH < NH3
Show answer

Answer: NH3 < (CH3)3N < CH3NH2 < (CH3)2NH

The basicity of amines in aqueous solution is influenced by two main factors: the +I effect of alkyl groups (which increases electron density on nitrogen, making it more available for protonation) and steric hindrance (which hinders the approach of a proton and solvation of the conjugate acid). In aqueous solution, the order is generally: Secondary amine > Primary amine > Tertiary amine > Ammonia. For methyl amines, the order is (CH3)2NH > CH3NH2 > (CH3)3N > NH3. So, the increasing order is NH3 < (CH3)3N < CH3NH2 < (CH3)2NH.

Question 40hard

Which of the following is NOT a characteristic of an ideal solution?

  1. ΔH_mix = 0
  2. ΔV_mix = 0
  3. Obeys Raoult's law over the entire range of concentration.
  4. Intermolecular forces between A-B are stronger than A-A and B-B.
Show answer

Answer: Intermolecular forces between A-B are stronger than A-A and B-B.

An ideal solution is characterized by: 1. ΔH_mix = 0 (no heat absorbed or released on mixing). 2. ΔV_mix = 0 (no change in volume on mixing). 3. It obeys Raoult's law at all concentrations and temperatures. 4. The intermolecular forces of attraction between the solute (A) and solvent (B) molecules are of the same magnitude as those between A-A and B-B molecules. If A-B forces are stronger than A-A and B-B, it would lead to a negative deviation from Raoult's law, characteristic of a non-ideal solution.

Question 41hard

Which of the following reactions represents the Kolbe's electrolytic reaction?

  1. R-COOH + NaOH → R-COONa + H2O
  2. 2R-COONa + 2H2O (electrolysis) → R-R + 2CO2 + 2NaOH + H2
  3. R-X + 2Na + X-R → R-R + 2NaX
  4. R-COOH + LiAlH4 → R-CH2OH
Show answer

Answer: 2R-COONa + 2H2O (electrolysis) → R-R + 2CO2 + 2NaOH + H2

Kolbe's electrolytic reaction involves the electrolysis of an aqueous solution of a sodium or potassium salt of a carboxylic acid to produce an alkane with an even number of carbon atoms. The general reaction is 2R-COONa + 2H2O (electrolysis) → R-R + 2CO2 + 2NaOH + H2.

Question 43hard

Which of the following is an example of a non-reducing sugar?

  1. Glucose
  2. Fructose
  3. Sucrose
  4. Maltose
Show answer

Answer: Sucrose

Non-reducing sugars do not have a free anomeric carbon (aldehyde or ketone group) available to reduce other compounds. Sucrose is a disaccharide formed by a glycosidic linkage between the anomeric carbon of glucose and the anomeric carbon of fructose, thus blocking both reducing ends. Glucose, fructose, and maltose all have free anomeric carbons and are therefore reducing sugars.

Question 44hard

Which of the following compounds will give a positive iodoform test?

  1. Propan-1-ol
  2. Propan-2-ol
  3. Ethanol
  4. Both B and C
Show answer

Answer: Both B and C

The iodoform test is given by compounds containing a CH₃CO- group or a CH₃CH(OH)- group. Propan-2-ol (CH₃CH(OH)CH₃) has the CH₃CH(OH)- group. Ethanol (CH₃CH₂OH) also has the CH₃CH(OH)- group (as it can be oxidized to acetaldehyde, CH₃CHO, which has the CH₃CO- group). Propan-1-ol (CH₃CH₂CH₂OH) does not have either of these groups. Therefore, both propan-2-ol and ethanol will give a positive iodoform test.

Question 45hard

The correct order of increasing basicity for the following amines is:

  1. CH₃NH₂ < (CH₃)₂NH < (CH₃)₃N < NH₃
  2. NH₃ < (CH₃)₃N < CH₃NH₂ < (CH₃)₂NH
  3. (CH₃)₃N < NH₃ < CH₃NH₂ < (CH₃)₂NH
  4. NH₃ < CH₃NH₂ < (CH₃)₂NH < (CH₃)₃N
Show answer

Answer: NH₃ < (CH₃)₃N < CH₃NH₂ < (CH₃)₂NH

The basicity of amines in aqueous solution is influenced by inductive effect (+I effect of alkyl groups), solvation effect, and steric hindrance. For methylamines in aqueous solution, the order of basicity is generally: Secondary amine > Primary amine > Tertiary amine > Ammonia. This is because the +I effect of two methyl groups in (CH₃)₂NH stabilizes the conjugate acid more effectively than one methyl group in CH₃NH₂. However, in (CH₃)₃N, steric hindrance by three methyl groups hinders the solvation of the protonated amine, making it less stable than the protonated primary and secondary amines. Therefore, the order is NH₃ < (CH₃)₃N < CH₃NH₂ < (CH₃)₂NH.

Question 46hard

Which of the following statements is true for a spontaneous reaction?

  1. ΔG > 0
  2. ΔG < 0
  3. ΔG = 0
  4. ΔH > 0
Show answer

Answer: ΔG < 0

For a reaction to be spontaneous under constant temperature and pressure, the change in Gibbs free energy (ΔG) must be negative (ΔG < 0). If ΔG > 0, the reaction is non-spontaneous. If ΔG = 0, the reaction is at equilibrium. ΔH (enthalpy change) being positive indicates an endothermic reaction, which can be spontaneous or non-spontaneous depending on the entropy change and temperature.

Question 47hard

The coordination number and oxidation state of Cr in K₃[Cr(C₂O₄)₃] are, respectively:

  1. 6, +3
  2. 3, +3
  3. 6, +2
  4. 3, +2
Show answer

Answer: 6, +3

In K₃[Cr(C₂O₄)₃], C₂O₄²⁻ (oxalate) is a bidentate ligand. Each oxalate ligand forms two coordinate bonds with the central metal ion. Since there are three oxalate ligands, the coordination number of Cr is 3 × 2 = 6. To find the oxidation state of Cr: Let the oxidation state of Cr be x. The charge on potassium (K) is +1, and there are three K atoms, so +3. The charge on oxalate (C₂O₄) is -2, and there are three oxalate ligands, so 3 × (-2) = -6. The overall complex is neutral. So, +3 + x + (-6) = 0 x - 3 = 0 x = +3 Therefore, the coordination number is 6 and the oxidation state is +3.

Question 48hard

Which of the following polymers is a polyamide?

  1. Teflon
  2. Nylon 6,6
  3. Polythene
  4. PVC
Show answer

Answer: Nylon 6,6

Polyamides are polymers containing amide linkages (-CO-NH-) in their backbone. Nylon 6,6 is a synthetic polyamide formed by the condensation polymerization of hexamethylenediamine and adipic acid. Teflon is a poly(tetrafluoroethene), polythene is poly(ethene), and PVC is poly(vinyl chloride); none of these contain amide linkages.

Question 49hard

An aqueous solution of a substance gives a white precipitate with AgNO₃ solution. The precipitate is soluble in excess NH₄OH. The substance is likely to be:

  1. NaCl
  2. NaBr
  3. NaI
  4. Na₂SO₄
Show answer

Answer: NaCl

This is a characteristic test for halide ions. When AgNO₃ is added to a solution containing halide ions, silver halides precipitate. - AgCl is a white precipitate, soluble in excess NH₄OH (forming [Ag(NH₃)₂]Cl). - AgBr is a pale yellow precipitate, sparingly soluble in excess NH₄OH. - AgI is a yellow precipitate, insoluble in excess NH₄OH. - Na₂SO₄ would give no precipitate with AgNO₃ (unless Ag₂SO₄ precipitates, which is sparingly soluble, but not a white precipitate soluble in NH₄OH in this context). Therefore, the substance is likely NaCl, as it forms a white precipitate (AgCl) that is soluble in excess NH₄OH.

Question 50hard

The rate constant of a first-order reaction is 2.303 × 10⁻³ s⁻¹. How long will it take for the concentration of the reactant to reduce to 1/10th of its initial value?

  1. 100 s
  2. 1000 s
  3. 2303 s
  4. 230.3 s
Show answer

Answer: 1000 s

For a first-order reaction, the integrated rate law is t = (2.303/k) log([A]₀/[A]). Given k = 2.303 × 10⁻³ s⁻¹ and [A] = [A]₀/10. So, [A]₀/[A] = 10. t = (2.303 / (2.303 × 10⁻³)) log(10) t = (1 / 10⁻³) × 1 t = 1000 s.

Question 51hard

An example of a solid solution in which the solute is a gas is:

  1. Brass
  2. Hydrogen in Palladium
  3. Copper dissolved in Gold
  4. Sugar in water
Show answer

Answer: Hydrogen in Palladium

A solid solution is a solid-state solution of one or more solutes in a solvent. In the case of hydrogen in palladium, hydrogen gas (solute) dissolves in solid palladium (solvent) to form a solid solution. Brass is a solid solution of two solids (copper and zinc). Copper dissolved in gold is also a solid solution of two solids. Sugar in water is a liquid solution.

Question 52hard

The correct order of increasing boiling points for the following compounds: CH₃CH₂OH, CH₃OCH₃, CH₃CH₂CH₃ is:

  1. CH₃OCH₃ < CH₃CH₂CH₃ < CH₃CH₂OH
  2. CH₃CH₂CH₃ < CH₃OCH₃ < CH₃CH₂OH
  3. CH₃CH₂OH < CH₃OCH₃ < CH₃CH₂CH₃
  4. CH₃CH₂CH₃ < CH₃CH₂OH < CH₃OCH₃
Show answer

Answer: CH₃CH₂CH₃ < CH₃OCH₃ < CH₃CH₂OH

Boiling points are influenced by intermolecular forces. CH₃CH₂CH₃ (propane) is an alkane and exhibits only weak London dispersion forces. CH₃OCH₃ (dimethyl ether) is an ether and has dipole-dipole interactions in addition to London dispersion forces. CH₃CH₂OH (ethanol) is an alcohol and can form strong hydrogen bonds, which are the strongest intermolecular forces among the three. Therefore, the order of increasing boiling points is CH₃CH₂CH₃ < CH₃OCH₃ < CH₃CH₂OH.

Question 53hard

The molar conductivity of a solution increases with dilution. This is because:

  1. The number of ions per unit volume increases.
  2. The degree of dissociation of the electrolyte decreases.
  3. The mobility of ions increases.
  4. The total number of ions in the solution increases for weak electrolytes.
Show answer

Answer: The total number of ions in the solution increases for weak electrolytes.

Molar conductivity (Λm) is defined as the conductivity of a solution containing one mole of electrolyte. For weak electrolytes, with dilution, the degree of dissociation (α) increases, leading to an increase in the total number of ions in the solution. For strong electrolytes, while the number of ions remains constant, the interionic attractions decrease, leading to increased ionic mobility. However, the most significant reason for the increase in molar conductivity with dilution, especially for weak electrolytes, is the increase in the number of ions due to enhanced dissociation.

Question 54hard

Which of the following amino acids is optically inactive?

  1. Glycine
  2. Alanine
  3. Valine
  4. Leucine
Show answer

Answer: Glycine

Optical activity in amino acids arises due to the presence of a chiral carbon atom (a carbon atom bonded to four different groups). Glycine is the only amino acid that does not have a chiral carbon atom because its alpha-carbon is bonded to two hydrogen atoms (in addition to an amino group, a carboxyl group, and an R-group which is also a hydrogen atom). Therefore, glycine is optically inactive.

Question 55hard

The reaction of primary amines with chloroform and alcoholic KOH is called:

  1. Wurtz reaction
  2. Carbylamine reaction
  3. Hoffmann bromamide degradation
  4. Gabriel phthalimide synthesis
Show answer

Answer: Carbylamine reaction

The reaction of primary amines (aliphatic or aromatic) with chloroform (CHCl₃) and alcoholic potassium hydroxide (KOH) to form isocyanides (carbylamines) is known as the Carbylamine reaction or Isocyanide test. This reaction is used as a test for primary amines. Wurtz reaction is for coupling alkyl halides, Hoffmann bromamide degradation converts amides to amines, and Gabriel phthalimide synthesis is for preparing primary amines.

Question 56hard

Which of the following is an example of a non-stoichiometric defect?

  1. Schottky defect
  2. Frenkel defect
  3. Metal excess defect
  4. Interstitial defect
Show answer

Answer: Metal excess defect

Non-stoichiometric defects are those in which the ratio of cations to anions becomes different from that indicated by the ideal chemical formula. Metal excess defect (due to anionic vacancies or presence of extra cations in interstitial sites) and metal deficiency defect are examples of non-stoichiometric defects. Schottky and Frenkel defects are stoichiometric defects, and interstitial defect can be stoichiometric (if atoms of the same type occupy interstitial sites) or non-stoichiometric (if extra cations occupy interstitial sites).

Question 57hard

Which of the following compounds will react with NaHCO₃ to produce CO₂ gas?

  1. Phenol
  2. Ethanol
  3. Acetic acid
  4. Aniline
Show answer

Answer: Acetic acid

Sodium bicarbonate (NaHCO₃) is a weak base. It reacts with acids stronger than carbonic acid (H₂CO₃) to produce CO₂ gas. Acetic acid is a carboxylic acid, which is stronger than carbonic acid, and thus reacts with NaHCO₃ to produce CO₂. Phenol is a weaker acid than carbonic acid, ethanol is an alcohol (very weak acid), and aniline is a base, so they will not react with NaHCO₃ to produce CO₂.

Question 58hard

The presence of which of the following elements in a compound can be detected by Lassaigne's test?

  1. Oxygen
  2. Sulphur
  3. Phosphorus
  4. All of these
Show answer

Answer: Sulphur

Lassaigne's test (sodium fusion test) is used to detect the presence of nitrogen, sulphur, halogens, and phosphorus in an organic compound. Oxygen is not detected by this test. Therefore, sulphur can be detected by Lassaigne's test.

Question 59hard

Which of the following is a biodegradable polymer?

  1. Polyethylene
  2. PVC
  3. Nylon-2-Nylon-6
  4. Teflon
Show answer

Answer: Nylon-2-Nylon-6

Biodegradable polymers are those that can be decomposed by microorganisms. Nylon-2-Nylon-6 is a polyamide copolymer of glycine (H₂N-CH₂-COOH) and aminocaproic acid (H₂N-(CH₂)₅-COOH), and it is a known example of a biodegradable polymer. Polyethylene, PVC, and Teflon are non-biodegradable synthetic polymers.

Question 60hard

The correct order of increasing acidic strength of the following compounds is: Phenol, Ethanol, Acetic acid, Water.

  1. Ethanol < Water < Phenol < Acetic acid
  2. Water < Ethanol < Phenol < Acetic acid
  3. Phenol < Ethanol < Water < Acetic acid
  4. Ethanol < Phenol < Water < Acetic acid
Show answer

Answer: Ethanol < Water < Phenol < Acetic acid

The acidic strength depends on the stability of the conjugate base formed after losing a proton. - Ethanol (CH₃CH₂OH) is a very weak acid, weaker than water, due to the electron-donating ethyl group. - Water (H₂O) is a neutral reference. - Phenol (C₆H₅OH) is more acidic than water and ethanol because its conjugate base (phenoxide ion) is resonance-stabilized. - Acetic acid (CH₃COOH) is the strongest among these because its conjugate base (acetate ion) is highly resonance-stabilized with two equivalent resonance structures, leading to effective delocalization of the negative charge. Therefore, the increasing order of acidic strength is: Ethanol < Water < Phenol < Acetic acid.

Question 61hard

Which of the following statements is INCORRECT regarding the properties of ideal solutions?

  1. ΔH_mix = 0
  2. ΔV_mix = 0
  3. Obeys Raoult's law over the entire range of concentration
  4. Intermolecular forces between A-B are stronger than A-A and B-B
Show answer

Answer: Intermolecular forces between A-B are stronger than A-A and B-B

For an ideal solution, the intermolecular forces of attraction between A-B components are equal to the average of the intermolecular forces between A-A and B-B components. If A-B forces were stronger, it would lead to a negative deviation from Raoult's law, and if weaker, a positive deviation. Therefore, the statement that A-B forces are stronger is incorrect for an ideal solution.

Question 62hard

The rate constant for a first-order reaction is 2.303 × 10⁻² s⁻¹. How long will it take for the concentration of the reactant to reduce to 1/10th of its initial value?

  1. 100 s
  2. 230.3 s
  3. 10 s
  4. 23.03 s
Show answer

Answer: 100 s

For a first-order reaction, the integrated rate law is given by t = (2.303/k) log([R]₀/[R]). Given k = 2.303 × 10⁻² s⁻¹ and [R] = [R]₀/10. So, t = (2.303 / (2.303 × 10⁻²)) log([R]₀ / ([R]₀/10)) t = (1 / 10⁻²) log(10) t = 100 × 1 t = 100 s

Question 63hard

The standard electrode potential (E°) for the Daniell cell is +1.1 V. Which of the following statements is correct regarding the spontaneity of the reaction?

  1. The reaction is non-spontaneous because E° is positive.
  2. The reaction is spontaneous because E° is positive.
  3. The reaction is at equilibrium because E° is positive.
  4. The spontaneity cannot be determined from E° alone.
Show answer

Answer: The reaction is spontaneous because E° is positive.

For an electrochemical cell, a positive standard electrode potential (E°_cell) indicates that the reaction is spontaneous under standard conditions. This is because ΔG° = -nFE°_cell, and for a spontaneous reaction, ΔG° must be negative. If E°_cell is positive, then ΔG° will be negative, making the reaction spontaneous.

Question 64hard

Which of the following amines will give a positive carbylamine test?

  1. Diethylamine
  2. N-methylaniline
  3. Aniline
  4. Triethylamine
Show answer

Answer: Aniline

The carbylamine test (also known as isocyanide test) is given by primary amines (both aliphatic and aromatic). In this test, the primary amine reacts with chloroform and alcoholic KOH to form an isocyanide (carbylamine), which has a foul smell. Aniline is a primary aromatic amine, hence it will give a positive carbylamine test. Diethylamine and N-methylaniline are secondary amines, and triethylamine is a tertiary amine; none of these will give a positive carbylamine test.

Question 65hard

Identify the product formed when glucose is reacted with concentrated nitric acid.

  1. Gluconic acid
  2. Saccharic acid
  3. Sorbitol
  4. Fructose
Show answer

Answer: Saccharic acid

When glucose is reacted with a mild oxidizing agent like bromine water, it oxidizes the aldehyde group to a carboxylic acid group, forming gluconic acid. However, when glucose is treated with a strong oxidizing agent like concentrated nitric acid, both the aldehyde group (-CHO) and the primary alcoholic group (-CH₂OH) at the other end are oxidized to carboxylic acid groups, resulting in the formation of saccharic acid (also known as glucaric acid).

Question 66hard

Which of the following is a characteristic property of transition elements?

  1. Exhibit only one oxidation state
  2. Form colorless compounds
  3. Have high ionization enthalpies
  4. Exhibit variable oxidation states
Show answer

Answer: Exhibit variable oxidation states

Transition elements are known for exhibiting variable oxidation states due to the participation of both (n-1)d and ns electrons in bonding. They also form colored compounds, have relatively lower ionization enthalpies compared to p-block elements, and are known for their catalytic properties and ability to form complexes.

Question 67hard

The IUPAC name of the complex [Co(NH₃)₅Cl]Cl₂ is:

  1. Pentamminechlorocobalt(III) chloride
  2. Chloropentamminecobalt(III) chloride
  3. Pentamminechlorocobalt(II) chloride
  4. Chloropentamminecobalt(II) chloride
Show answer

Answer: Pentamminechlorocobalt(III) chloride

In naming coordination compounds, ligands are named first in alphabetical order, followed by the central metal atom. The oxidation state of the metal is indicated by Roman numerals in parentheses. Anionic ligands end in -o (e.g., chloro for Cl⁻), and neutral ligands are named as such (e.g., ammine for NH₃). The complex ion is [Co(NH₃)₅Cl]²⁺. Let the oxidation state of Co be x. x + 5(0) + (-1) = +2, so x = +3. Thus, the name is Pentamminechlorocobalt(III) chloride.

Question 68hard

Which of the following reagents can be used to distinguish between phenol and ethanol?

  1. Sodium metal
  2. FeCl₃ solution
  3. Lucas reagent
  4. Tollens' reagent
Show answer

Answer: FeCl₃ solution

Phenol gives a characteristic violet/purple/green coloration with neutral ferric chloride (FeCl₃) solution due to the formation of a complex. Ethanol does not react with FeCl₃ solution in this manner. Both phenol and ethanol react with sodium metal. Lucas reagent is used to distinguish between primary, secondary, and tertiary alcohols. Tollens' reagent is used to detect aldehydes.

Question 70hard

  3. Salicylaldehyde
  4. Benzoic acid

Question 71hard

Which of the following reagents would distinguish between propanal and propanone?

  1. Tollens' reagent
  2. Fehling's solution
  3. Iodoform test
  4. Both A and B
Show answer

Answer: Both A and B

Propanal is an aldehyde, while propanone is a ketone. Aldehydes give positive tests with Tollens' reagent (silver mirror) and Fehling's solution (red precipitate of Cu₂O), while ketones generally do not. Therefore, both Tollens' reagent and Fehling's solution can distinguish between them. The iodoform test would be positive for propanone (methyl ketone) but not for propanal.

Question 72hard

The correct order of increasing basicity of the following amines is:

  1. NH₃ < C₆H₅NH₂ < (CH₃)₂NH < CH₃NH₂
  2. C₆H₅NH₂ < NH₃ < CH₃NH₂ < (CH₃)₂NH
  3. C₆H₅NH₂ < CH₃NH₂ < (CH₃)₂NH < NH₃
  4. NH₃ < CH₃NH₂ < (CH₃)₂NH < C₆H₅NH₂
Show answer

Answer: C₆H₅NH₂ < NH₃ < CH₃NH₂ < (CH₃)₂NH

The basicity of amines depends on the availability of the lone pair of electrons on the nitrogen atom. Electron-donating groups (like alkyl groups) increase basicity, while electron-withdrawing groups (like phenyl group) decrease basicity. In aqueous solution, the order of basicity for methylamines is generally (CH₃)₂NH > CH₃NH₂ > NH₃. Aniline (C₆H₅NH₂) is the least basic due to the resonance stabilization of the lone pair of electrons with the benzene ring, making it less available for protonation. Thus, the correct order is C₆H₅NH₂ < NH₃ < CH₃NH₂ < (CH₃)₂NH.

Question 73hard

What is the oxidation state of Fe in [Fe(CN)₆]³⁻?

  1. +2
  2. +3
  3. +4
  4. +6
Show answer

Answer: +3

Let the oxidation state of Fe be x. The cyanide ligand (CN⁻) has a charge of -1. There are six cyanide ligands. The overall charge of the complex ion is -3. So, x + 6(-1) = -3 x - 6 = -3 x = -3 + 6 x = +3. Therefore, the oxidation state of Fe in [Fe(CN)₆]³⁻ is +3.

Question 74hard

Which of the following reagents would you use for the conversion of a primary alcohol to an aldehyde?

  1. K₂Cr₂O₇/H₂SO₄
  2. KMnO₄/H⁺
  3. PCC (Pyridinium Chlorochromate)
  4. CrO₃/H₂SO₄ (Jones reagent)
Show answer

Answer: PCC (Pyridinium Chlorochromate)

To convert a primary alcohol to an aldehyde, a mild oxidizing agent is required to prevent further oxidation to a carboxylic acid. PCC (Pyridinium Chlorochromate) is a selective oxidizing agent that oxidizes primary alcohols to aldehydes and secondary alcohols to ketones without further oxidation. K₂Cr₂O₇/H₂SO₄, KMnO₄/H⁺, and CrO₃/H₂SO₄ (Jones reagent) are strong oxidizing agents that would oxidize primary alcohols directly to carboxylic acids.

Question 75hard

The half-life period of a radioactive substance is 20 minutes. What fraction of the original amount will remain after 1 hour?

  1. 1/2
  2. 1/4
  3. 1/8
  4. 1/16
Show answer

Answer: 1/8

The half-life (t₁/₂) is 20 minutes. The total time is 1 hour = 60 minutes. Number of half-lives (n) = Total time / Half-life = 60 min / 20 min = 3. The fraction remaining after 'n' half-lives is (1/2)ⁿ. So, fraction remaining = (1/2)³ = 1/8.

Question 76hard

Which of the following elements does NOT exhibit allotropy?

  1. Carbon
  2. Sulphur
  3. Nitrogen
  4. Phosphorus
Show answer

Answer: Nitrogen

Allotropy is the property of some chemical elements to exist in two or more different forms, in the same physical state. Carbon (diamond, graphite, fullerenes), Sulphur (rhombic, monoclinic), and Phosphorus (white, red, black) all exhibit allotropy. Nitrogen, however, does not exhibit allotropy under normal conditions.

Question 77hard

The correct order of increasing boiling points for the following compounds is:

  1. CH3CH2CH3 < CH3OCH3 < CH3CH2OH
  2. CH3OCH3 < CH3CH2CH3 < CH3CH2OH
  3. CH3CH2OH < CH3OCH3 < CH3CH2CH3
  4. CH3CH2CH3 < CH3CH2OH < CH3OCH3
Show answer

Answer: CH3CH2CH3 < CH3OCH3 < CH3CH2OH

Boiling points are influenced by intermolecular forces. CH3CH2CH3 (propane) is an alkane and exhibits only weak London dispersion forces. CH3OCH3 (dimethyl ether) is an ether and has dipole-dipole interactions, which are stronger than London dispersion forces. CH3CH2OH (ethanol) is an alcohol and can form strong hydrogen bonds, which are the strongest intermolecular forces among the given compounds. Therefore, the order of increasing boiling points is CH3CH2CH3 < CH3OCH3 < CH3CH2OH.

Question 78hard

Which of the following is a characteristic of a lyophilic colloid?

  1. Irreversible in nature
  2. Easily coagulated by adding small amounts of electrolytes
  3. High stability
  4. Low viscosity
Show answer

Answer: High stability

Lyophilic colloids are 'solvent-loving' and are quite stable due to strong attractive forces between the dispersed phase and the dispersion medium. They are reversible, not easily coagulated by electrolytes, and generally have high viscosity. Lyophobic colloids, on the other hand, are irreversible, easily coagulated, and less stable.

Question 79hard

The oxidation state of Fe in [Fe(CN)6]³⁻ is:

  1. +2
  2. +3
  3. +4
  4. +6
Show answer

Answer: +3

Let the oxidation state of Fe be x. The cyanide ligand (CN⁻) has a charge of -1. There are 6 cyanide ligands. The overall charge of the complex ion is -3. So, x + 6(-1) = -3. x - 6 = -3. x = -3 + 6. x = +3. Therefore, the oxidation state of Fe is +3.

Question 80hard

Which of the following statements is true about the order of a reaction?

  1. It can only be a whole number.
  2. It is always equal to the molecularity of the reaction.
  3. It can be determined experimentally only.
  4. It is always equal to the sum of the stoichiometric coefficients of the reactants.
Show answer

Answer: It can be determined experimentally only.

The order of a reaction is an experimentally determined quantity. It can be a whole number, a fraction, or even zero. It is not necessarily equal to the molecularity, which is the number of reacting species taking part in an elementary reaction. The sum of stoichiometric coefficients gives the molecularity for an elementary reaction, but not necessarily the order for a complex reaction.

Question 81hard

For a first-order reaction, the time required for 99% completion is how many times the time required for 90% completion?

  1. 1.5 times
  2. 2 times
  3. 3 times
  4. 4 times
Show answer

Answer: 2 times

For a first-order reaction, the integrated rate law is given by t = (2.303/k) log([A]₀/[A]). For 90% completion, [A] = [A]₀ - 0.90[A]₀ = 0.10[A]₀. t_90% = (2.303/k) log([A]₀/0.10[A]₀) = (2.303/k) log(10) = (2.303/k) * 1. For 99% completion, [A] = [A]₀ - 0.99[A]₀ = 0.01[A]₀. t_99% = (2.303/k) log([A]₀/0.01[A]₀) = (2.303/k) log(100) = (2.303/k) * 2. Comparing the two, t_99% / t_90% = ((2.303/k) * 2) / ((2.303/k) * 1) = 2. Therefore, the time required for 99% completion is 2 times the time required for 90% completion.

Question 82hard

Which of the following compounds will react with Lucas reagent (conc. HCl + anhydrous ZnCl₂) most rapidly?

  1. CH₃CH₂OH
  2. (CH₃)₂CHOH
  3. (CH₃)₃COH
  4. CH₃OH
Show answer

Answer: (CH₃)₃COH

Lucas reagent is used to distinguish between primary, secondary, and tertiary alcohols. The reaction involves the formation of an alkyl chloride, which appears as turbidity. The reactivity order is tertiary > secondary > primary alcohols. Tertiary alcohols react immediately to produce turbidity due to the formation of a stable tertiary carbocation intermediate. Secondary alcohols react within 5-10 minutes, while primary alcohols react only upon heating. (CH₃)₃COH is a tertiary alcohol, (CH₃)₂CHOH is a secondary alcohol, CH₃CH₂OH is a primary alcohol, and CH₃OH is methanol (a primary alcohol).

Question 83hard

The correct order of increasing basicity for the following amines in aqueous solution is:

  1. CH₃NH₂ < (CH₃)₃N < (CH₃)₂NH
  2. (CH₃)₃N < CH₃NH₂ < (CH₃)₂NH
  3. (CH₃)₂NH < CH₃NH₂ < (CH₃)₃N
  4. CH₃NH₂ < (CH₃)₂NH < (CH₃)₃N
Show answer

Answer: (CH₃)₃N < CH₃NH₂ < (CH₃)₂NH

The basicity of amines in aqueous solution is influenced by a combination of factors: the +I effect of alkyl groups (electron-donating, increasing electron density on nitrogen), steric hindrance (hindering protonation), and solvation effects (stabilization of the conjugate acid by hydrogen bonding with water). For methyl-substituted amines in aqueous solution, the order of basicity is generally: Secondary amine > Primary amine > Tertiary amine > Ammonia. This is because the +I effect of two methyl groups in (CH₃)₂NH is greater than one in CH₃NH₂, but in (CH₃)₃N, the increased steric hindrance and reduced solvation of the protonated amine outweigh the +I effect of three methyl groups. Therefore, the correct order is (CH₃)₃N < CH₃NH₂ < (CH₃)₂NH.

Question 84hard

Which of the following is an example of a condensation polymer?

  1. Polyethylene
  2. Teflon
  3. Nylon 6,6
  4. Polyvinyl chloride (PVC)
Show answer

Answer: Nylon 6,6

Condensation polymers are formed by the head-to-tail joining of monomers with the elimination of small molecules like water, alcohol, or HCl. Nylon 6,6 is formed by the condensation polymerization of hexamethylenediamine and adipic acid, with the elimination of water molecules. Polyethylene, Teflon, and PVC are all examples of addition polymers, formed by the direct addition of monomers without the loss of any small molecules.

Answer: It is a measure of the equilibrium constant with a value of 2.0

The equilibrium constant (Kc) is a measure of the equilibrium constant, and the given value is an example of this concept.

Question 367easy

Answer: Twice the specific heat capacity

Question 512medium

Which of the following statements is true about the reaction of a weak acid with a strong base?

  1. The resulting solution is acidic
  2. The resulting solution is basic
  3. The resulting solution is neutral
  4. The resulting solution is amphoteric
Show answer

Answer: The resulting solution is basic

The reaction of a weak acid with a strong base results in a basic solution. This is because the strong base completely dissociates and the weak acid only partially dissociates.

Question 513medium

  1. The resulting solution is acidic
  2. The resulting solution is basic
  3. The resulting solution is neutral
  4. The resulting solution is amphoteric
Show answer

Answer: The resulting solution is neutral

The reaction of a strong acid with a strong base results in a neutral solution. This is because both the strong acid and the strong base completely dissociate and the resulting ions combine to form a neutral salt and water.

Question 515medium

  3. Immiscibility
  4. Constant Density

Answer: Constant Boiling Point

Azeotropes form due to the constant boiling point of the mixture. This occurs when the vapor pressure of the mixture is equal to the sum of the vapor pressures of the individual components.

Show answer

Answer: Increases the rate

A catalyst increases the rate of a chemical reaction by providing an alternative reaction pathway with lower activation energy. This allows the reaction to proceed faster than it would without the catalyst.

  2. IF > BrF > ClF
  3. BrF > ClF > IF
  4. ClF < BrF < IF
Show answer

Answer: ClF > BrF > IF

The reactivity of interhalogen compounds decreases from ClF to IF.

The minimum energy required for a chemical reaction to occur at a given pressure is still referred to as activation energy.

Question 1003medium

Which of the following statements is true about the effect of decreasing pressure on the equilibrium of a reaction with 3 moles of gas on the product side?

  1. Shifts to the Left
  2. Shifts to the Right
  3. No Effect
  4. Reversible
Show answer

Answer: Shifts to the Left

According to Le Chatelier's principle, decreasing pressure will shift the equilibrium to the side with more moles of gas, which in this case is the reactant side, so the reaction shifts to the left.

Question 1004medium

Which of the following statements is true about the effect of increasing pressure on the equilibrium of a reaction with 2 moles of gas on the reactant side?

  1. Shifts to the Left
  2. Shifts to the Right
  3. No Effect
  4. Reversible
Show answer

Answer: Shifts to the Right

According to Le Chatelier's principle, increasing pressure will shift the equilibrium to the side with fewer moles of gas, which in this case is the product side, so the reaction shifts to the right.

Question 1005medium

Which of the following statements is true about the effect of increasing pressure on the equilibrium of a reaction with equal moles of gas on both sides?

  1. Shifts to the Left
  2. Shifts to the Right
  3. No Effect
  4. Reversible
Show answer

Answer: No Effect

According to Le Chatelier's principle, if the number of moles of gas is equal on both sides, changing the pressure will have no effect on the equilibrium.

Question 1083hard

  1. Only molecular compounds form crystals
  2. Only covalent compounds form crystals
  3. Only ionic compounds form crystals
  4. Both ionic and molecular compounds can form crystals

Answer: Only ionic compounds form crystals
